من فقير، ويجوز دفع ما على جماعة لواحد على الصحيح. والله الموفق للصواب.
وعن مماليكه للخدمة: أطلقه فشمل المديون والمستأجر والمرهون إذا كان عنده وفاء بالدين، والعبد الجاني عمدا كان أو خطأ، والعبد المنذور بالتصدق به، والعبد المعلق عتقه بمجيء يوم الفطر والعبد الموصى برقبته لإنسان وبخدمته لآخر، فإنها على الموصى له بالرقبة بخلاف النفقة فإنها على الموصى له بالخدمة وأشار بقوله: "للخدمة" إلى أنه لا يخرج عن عبده الآبق ولا عن المغصوب المجحود إلا بعد عوده فيلزمه لما مضى، ولا عن عبده المأسور؛
لأنه خارج عن يده وتصرفه، فأشبه المكاتب ولا عن . خادمه بإجارة أو إعارة البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٤٠٠/١] و مدبره المدبر مملوك قال له :مولاه أنت معتق عن دبر مني مثلا وأم ولده أم الولد: أمة ولدت ولدنا من مولاها، وادعى المولى نسبه ولو كفارا أي ولو كان لهؤلاء كافرين وقن مشترك أي لا يؤديها عن عبد بين شريكين فصاعدا ما يحتاجه أي من هذه الأصناف التي تخرج منها الفطرة بأن كان الزمن زمن حب. وصح لو قدم أشار بإطلاقه إلى أن لا تفصيل بين مدة ومدة كما في "الهداية"، وهو الصحيح، وعند خلف بن أيوب: يجوز تعجيلها بعد دخول رمضان لا قبله وقيل يجوز تعجيلها في النصف الأخير من رمضان، وقيل: في العشر الأخير، وعند الحسن بن زياد لا يجوز تعجيلها أصلا كالأضحية وتسقط بمضي يوم الفطر؛ لأنها قربة اختصت بيوم العيد، فتسقط بمضيه، كالأضحية تسقط بمضي أيام النحر، قلنا: إنها قربة مالية لا تسقط بعد الوجوب إلا بالأداء كالزكاة والأضحية لا تسقط ولكن ينتقل الوجوب إلى التصدق بالقيمة؛ وهذا لأن القربة في إراقة الدم غير معقولة، وإنما عرفت شرعا في أيام مخصوصة، ووجه القربة في التصدق بالمال معقول، خلة المحتاج، فلا يقدر وقت الأداء فيه بوقت [الكفاية بزيادة: ٢٣٢/٢] وهو
Sadaqat al-Fitr. Book of Zakat: And concerning his slaves for service, and his mudabbar, and his umm walad, even if they are disbelievers, not concerning his mukatab, nor concerning his adult son and his daughter. He said: i.e., he does not pay. And his wife, and a jointly owned slave, and a runaway slave except after his return, and likewise the usurped and the captive. And it is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or its groats, or a sa' of dates, raisins, or barley, and it is eight ratls by Iraqi measure. i.e., the poor person. And it is permissible to pay the value, and it is better when he finds what he needs because it is quicker to satisfy the need of the poor. And if it is a time of hardship, then wheat, barley, and what is eaten are better than dirhams. And the time of obligation is at the dawn of the day of Fitr. Whoever dies or becomes poor before it, or embraces Islam, or becomes rich, or is born after it, it is not obligatory upon him. He became rich. And it is recommended to give it before going out to the prayer place. And it is valid if he gives it early or late, but delay is disliked. And each person gives his fitr to one poor person. And there is disagreement on the permissibility of dividing one fitr among more than one poor person. And it is permissible to give what is upon a group to one person according to the correct opinion. And Allah is the giver of success. And concerning his slaves for service: he made it absolute, so it includes the indebted, the hired, and the mortgaged if he has enough to pay off the debt, and the slave who commits a crime intentionally or unintentionally, and the slave vowed to be given in charity, and the slave whose freedom is conditional on the arrival of the day of Fitr, and the slave whose ownership is bequeathed to one person and his service to another. The fitr is upon the legatee of the ownership, unlike maintenance which is upon the legatee of the service. And he indicated by his saying "for service" that he does not pay for his runaway slave, nor for the usurped and denied slave except after his return, in which case it becomes obligatory for the past period, nor for his captive slave, because he is outside his control and disposition, so he is like the mukatab. Nor for his hired or lent servant. Bahr al-Raiq with adaptation: 400/1]. And mudabbar: a mudabbar slave is one to whom his master said: You are free after my death, for example. And umm walad: a female slave who gave birth to a child from her master, and the master claimed the child's lineage, even if they are disbelievers. i.e., even if these are disbelievers. And a jointly owned slave: i.e., he does not pay it for a slave between two or more partners. What he needs: i.e., from these types from which fitr is given, meaning when the time is a time of love. And "it is valid if he gives early" — he indicated by its absoluteness that there is no distinction between one period and another, as in al-Hidayah, and this is correct. According to Khalf ibn Ayyub: it is permissible to give it early after the entry of Ramadan, not before. And it was said: it is permissible to give it early in the last half of Ramadan. And it was said: in the last ten days. According to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad: it is not permissible to give it early at all, like the udhiyah, and it lapses with the passing of the day of Fitr, because it is an act of worship specific to the day of Eid, so it lapses with its passing, like the udhiyah lapses with the passing of the days of sacrifice. We said: it is a financial act of worship that does not lapse after obligation except by fulfillment, like zakat. The udhiyah does not lapse, but the obligation transfers to giving charity with the value. This is because the worship in shedding blood is not rationally understood; it is only known legislatively in specific days. The aspect of worship in giving charity with wealth is rationally understood: the need of the poor. So the time of performance is not restricted to a specific time. [al-Kifaya with addition: 232/2] And it is
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rulings of Sadaqat al-Fitr (Zakat al-Fitr). It states the categories of people for whom the head of household must pay fitr: his slaves for service, mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred after master's death), umm walad (concubine who bore his child), even if they are non-Muslim. He does not pay for a mukatab (slave who has contracted freedom for payment) nor for his adult son and daughter. The fitr is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or groats, or a sa' of dates, raisins, or barley, which equals eight Iraqi ratls. Paying the monetary value is permissible and considered better in normal times because it satisfies the poor's need faster, but in times of scarcity, grain is better. The obligation begins at dawn of Eid al-Fitr. If someone dies or becomes poor before that, or accepts Islam, or becomes rich, or a child is born after, the fitr is not obligatory. It is recommended to give it before going to the Eid prayer, but early or delayed payment is valid, though delay is disliked. One person's fitr should be given to one poor person, but it is permissible to give the fitr of a group to one person. The commentary then provides detailed discussion on slaves: it includes indebted hired, mortgaged, criminal, vowed, conditionally freed, and those with split ownership/bequest. For a runaway or usurped slave, fitr is only due after return. A captive slave is not paid for because he is like a mukatab. The passage also includes a debate among Hanafi scholars about early payment: some permit after Ramadan begins, others only in the last half or last ten days, while al-Hasan ibn Ziyad forbids early payment completely, analogizing to udhiyah which lapses after its time. The counter-argument is that fitr is a financial worship like zakat, which does not lapse; udhiyah is different because its rationale (shedding blood) is not rational, while fitr's rationale (relieving need) is continuous. Thus, if not given on time, the obligation transfers to giving the value as charity.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (Sadaqat al-Fitr): A wajib charity distributed at the end of Ramadan to purify the fasting person's shortcomings and help the poor.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free after the master's death.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child recognized by the master; she becomes free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, for which type of slave does the master NOT have to pay Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Mudabbar
B) Umm walad
C) Mukatab
D) Slave for service

Key Takeaway
The core obligations of Sadaqat al-Fitr include specific beneficiaries, a fixed measure, and a defined time of obligation, with the option of paying value.

Zakat — Almsgiving
advanced
12 min
The Dispute on Early Payment and Lapsing of Sadaqat al-Fitr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on early payment and lapsing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on early payment of Sadaqat al-Fitr and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether it lapses after Eid.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr does not lapse after Eid; it remains a debt because its rationale is the ongoing need of the poor.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah addresses a contested issue within the Hanafi school: can Sadaqat al-Fitr be given before Eid, and does it lapse if delayed? The commentary presents the majority view that early payment is unrestricted and that the obligation continues like a debt. We will analyze the proofs and the opposing argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing views
Khalf ibn Ayyub allows early payment after Ramadan begins; some allow last half or ten days; al-Hasan ibn Ziyad forbids early entirely and claims lapsing.
Al-Hasan's view is the strongest opposition.
2
State the Hanafi majority position
Early payment is valid without time restriction, and the obligation does not lapse.
The text says 'صح لو قدم أو أخر' and commentary from al-Hidayah affirms no distinction.
3
Analyze the proof for the majority
Sadaqat al-Fitr is a financial worship (qurba maliyya) analogous to zakat, which does not lapse. The rationale (illa) is the poor's need, which is continuous.
The argument uses qiyas on zakat.
4
Contrast with the opposing analogy
Al-Hasan compares fitr to udhiyah, which lapses after its appointed days because its rationale (bloodshed) is not rationally understood and is time-bound.
The Hanafi response distinguishes based on rational vs. non-rational worship.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If delayed, the majority says it must still be given (as value), while al-Hasan's view would say no obligation remains.
Practical consequence: one must pay even if a year passes.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the rulings of Sadaqat al-Fitr (Zakat al-Fitr). It states the categories of people for whom the head of household must pay fitr: his slaves for service, mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred after master's death), umm walad (concubine who bore his child), even if they are non-Muslim. Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jil): Early payment of an obligation before its due time.
أضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal offered on the days of Eid al-Adha.
قربة مالية (qurba maliyya): An act of worship involving the expenditure of wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr does not lapse after Eid; early payment is unrestricted, and if delayed, the obligation remains as a debt.
